<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">List of wettest tropical cyclones by country</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p>This is a <b>list of wettest tropical cyclones by country</b>, using all known available sources. Data is most complete for Australia, Cuba, Dominican Republic, Japan, Hong Kong, Mexico, Taiwan, Yap, Chuuk, and the United States, with fragmentary data available for other countries. The <a href="/wiki/Overseas_department" title="Overseas department">French region</a> of <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="Réunion">Réunion</a> holds several world records for tropical cyclone and worldwide rainfall, due to the rough topography and its proximity to the Indian Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Global_tropical_cyclone_tracks-edit2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="8000" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Global_tropical_cyclone_tracks-edit2.jpg/250px-Global_tropical_cyclone_tracks-edit2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Global_tropical_cyclone_tracks-edit2.jpg/375px-Global_tropical_cyclone_tracks-edit2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Global_tropical_cyclone_tracks-edit2.jpg/500px-Global_tropical_cyclone_tracks-edit2.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Global_tropical_cyclone_tracks-edit2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A map of all tropical cyclone tracks, encompassing the period between the years 1985 and 2005.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Below are the records for each country above.</p>
<p></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Christmas_Island">Christmas Island</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Christmas Island">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gillian_Mar_22_2014_0310Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6900" data-file-width="6200" height="245" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Gillian_Mar_22_2014_0310Z.jpg/220px-Gillian_Mar_22_2014_0310Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Gillian_Mar_22_2014_0310Z.jpg/330px-Gillian_Mar_22_2014_0310Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Gillian_Mar_22_2014_0310Z.jpg/440px-Gillian_Mar_22_2014_0310Z.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gillian_Mar_22_2014_0310Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cyclone Gillian</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Christmas_Island" title="Christmas Island">Christmas Island</a> is an Australian territory located in the Indian Ocean located at the summit of a submarine mountain, which rises steeply to a central plateau that is dominated by stands of rainforest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C.26C_islands_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-C.26C_islands-14">[14]</a></sup> After rainfall and wind observations started on the island during 1972, only 13 tropical cyclones passed within 220 km (135 mi) of the territory between 1972 and 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C.26C_islands_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-C.26C_islands-14">[14]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cocos_Islands">Cocos Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Cocos Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:11U_Feb_25_2013_0350Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="9825" data-file-width="8553" height="253" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/11U_Feb_25_2013_0350Z.jpg/220px-11U_Feb_25_2013_0350Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/11U_Feb_25_2013_0350Z.jpg/330px-11U_Feb_25_2013_0350Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/11U_Feb_25_2013_0350Z.jpg/440px-11U_Feb_25_2013_0350Z.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:11U_Feb_25_2013_0350Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Although Tropical Low 11U in 2013 remained more than 120 km (75 mi) away from the Cocos Islands, wind shear displaced convection westward and over the islands for several days, resulting in record breaking rainfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11U_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-11U-21">[21]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cocos_(Keeling)_Islands" title="Cocos (Keeling) Islands">Cocos (Keeling) Islands</a> are an Australian territory of 27 coral islands that are formed into two large coral atolls and cover an area of around 36 km<sup>2</sup> (14 sq mi) of the Indian Ocean to the northwest of Perth, Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C.26C_islands_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-C.26C_islands-14">[14]</a></sup> Rainfall observations started on the islands during 1907, while temperature, wind and other records started in 1952.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C.26C_islands_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-C.26C_islands-14">[14]</a></sup> Between 1952 and 2005 27 tropical cyclones caused storm force wind gusts of over 90 km/h (55 mph) on the islands, while only four caused hurricane-force gusts of over 125 km/h (80 mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C.26C_islands_14-4"><a href="#cite_note-C.26C_islands-14">[14]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Bangladesh">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:02B_2015-07-29_0500Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7800" data-file-width="6000" height="286" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/02B_2015-07-29_0500Z.jpg/220px-02B_2015-07-29_0500Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/02B_2015-07-29_0500Z.jpg/330px-02B_2015-07-29_0500Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/02B_2015-07-29_0500Z.jpg/440px-02B_2015-07-29_0500Z.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:02B_2015-07-29_0500Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cyclone Komen approaching Bangladesh on July 29, 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bangladesh has been the scene of the greatest tropical cyclone casualties in recent times. The country is quite flat and generally lies near sea level.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Belize">Belize</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Belize">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This country has terrain mainly across its southern sections, with elevations up to about 3,700 feet (1,100 m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> The highest reported rainfall in what was formerly British Honduras occurred during <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Keith" title="Hurricane Keith">Hurricane Keith</a> in 2000 when 32.67 inches (830 mm) of rain fell in a 24‑hour period at Phillip Goodson International Airport in <a href="/wiki/Belize_City" title="Belize City">Belize City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Keith_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Keith-49">[49]</a></sup> It should be noted that equally heavy rains could have fallen during <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hattie" title="Hurricane Hattie">Hurricane Hattie</a> of 1961 and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Fifi" title="Hurricane Fifi">Hurricane Fifi</a> of 1974.</p>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Keith_30_sept_2000_2227Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1120" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Hurricane_Keith_30_sept_2000_2227Z.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Keith_30_sept_2000_2227Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Hurricane_Keith_30_sept_2000_2227Z.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Keith_30_sept_2000_2227Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Hurricane_Keith_30_sept_2000_2227Z.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Keith_30_sept_2000_2227Z.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Keith_30_sept_2000_2227Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:144px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Harvey1999092306GOES8IR.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="134" data-file-width="142" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/c1/Harvey1999092306GOES8IR.jpg" width="142"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Harvey1999092306GOES8IR.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Extratropical cyclone Harvey near Nova Scotia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Tropical cyclones are usually in transition to <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclones</a> by the time they reach <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Canada" title="Atlantic Canada">Atlantic Canada</a>, though occasionally they retain their tropical status. No tropical cyclone has ever hit Canada's Pacific coast.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/China_tropical_cyclone_rainfall_climatology" title="China tropical cyclone rainfall climatology">China tropical cyclone rainfall climatology</a></div>
<p>China is a mountainous country, which leads to rapid dissipation of cyclones that move inland as well as significant amounts of rain from those dissipating cyclones. <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Nina_(1975)" title="Typhoon Nina (1975)">Typhoon Nina (1975)</a> caused the collapse of two huge reservoirs and ten smaller dams when 1,062 millimetres (41.8 in) fell in <a href="/wiki/Henan" title="Henan">Henan</a> during a 24‑hour period, which is the record for Mainland China. Typhoon Sam of the <a href="/wiki/1999_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="1999 Pacific typhoon season">1999 Pacific typhoon season</a> became the wettest known tropical cyclone to impact Hong Kong since records began in 1884, breaking a 73‑year‑old record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Precipitation associated with tropical cyclones and their remains can bring snow to <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a>. An early October 2004 tropical depression brought daily precipitation of 6 centimetres (2.4 in) of liquid equivalent precipitation to Che-Ku county in the form of heavy snow, which was a new October daily precipitation record for both rain and snow. This led to a loss of 340,000 kg of food, 230,000 kg of forage grass, and 263 livestock in the snowstorm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PADGETTOCT2004_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTOCT2004-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Soudelor_2015-08-08_0525Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="9400" data-file-width="7200" height="287" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Soudelor_2015-08-08_0525Z.jpg/220px-Soudelor_2015-08-08_0525Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Soudelor_2015-08-08_0525Z.jpg/330px-Soudelor_2015-08-08_0525Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Soudelor_2015-08-08_0525Z.jpg/440px-Soudelor_2015-08-08_0525Z.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Soudelor_2015-08-08_0525Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Typhoon Soudelor/Hanna</div>
</div>
</div>

<h3><span id="Taiwan/Taipei"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Taiwan.2FTaipei">Taiwan/Taipei</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Taiwan/Taipei">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The mountainous island of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> province experiences an average of 1.8 tropical cyclone landfalls each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BAMSapr2009_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-BAMSapr2009-80">[80]</a></sup> Due to its rugged topography, Taiwan sees extreme rains from tropical cyclones, particularly in its central mountain range.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_Morakot_Aug_7_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="9200" data-file-width="7200" height="281" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Typhoon_Morakot_Aug_7_2009.jpg/220px-Typhoon_Morakot_Aug_7_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Typhoon_Morakot_Aug_7_2009.jpg/330px-Typhoon_Morakot_Aug_7_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Typhoon_Morakot_Aug_7_2009.jpg/440px-Typhoon_Morakot_Aug_7_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_Morakot_Aug_7_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba">Cuba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Cuba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Flora" title="Hurricane Flora">Hurricane Flora</a> of October 1963 drifted across Cuba for four days, leading to extreme rainfall across the mountainous island country. During the heaviest 24‑hour period of rainfall, 735 millimetres (28.9 in) of rain fell at <a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Cuba" title="Santiago de Cuba">Santiago de Cuba</a>. Total amounts of 2,033 millimetres (80.0 in) over 4 days and 2,550 millimetres (100 in) over 5 days produced staggering loss of life in Cuba, where over 2000 perished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CUBARAIN_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-CUBARAIN-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Dennis_on_July_7_2005_1550_UTC.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7200" data-file-width="5600" height="283" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Hurricane_Dennis_on_July_7_2005_1550_UTC.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Dennis_on_July_7_2005_1550_UTC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Hurricane_Dennis_on_July_7_2005_1550_UTC.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Dennis_on_July_7_2005_1550_UTC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Hurricane_Dennis_on_July_7_2005_1550_UTC.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Dennis_on_July_7_2005_1550_UTC.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dominica">Dominica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Dominica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Erika_2015-08-27_1725Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7800" data-file-width="6000" height="286" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Erika_2015-08-27_1725Z.jpg/220px-Erika_2015-08-27_1725Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Erika_2015-08-27_1725Z.jpg/330px-Erika_2015-08-27_1725Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Erika_2015-08-27_1725Z.jpg/440px-Erika_2015-08-27_1725Z.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Erika_2015-08-27_1725Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Erika near Dominica</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The islands of the eastern <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> are constantly threatened by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_storm" title="Tropical storm">tropical storms</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane" title="Hurricane">hurricanes</a>, mainly between August and October. Dominica is a rugged island, with spots of elevation as high as nearly 4,750 feet (1,450 m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> As <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jeanne" title="Hurricane Jeanne">Hurricane Jeanne</a> moved through the region, 422.3 millimetres (16.63 in) of rain fell during the 24‑hour period ending on the morning of September 15, 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PADGETTSEP2004_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTSEP2004-40">[40]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dominican_Republic">Dominican Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Dominican Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Noel_28_oct_2007_1530Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7800" data-file-width="6000" height="286" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Noel_28_oct_2007_1530Z.jpg/220px-Noel_28_oct_2007_1530Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Noel_28_oct_2007_1530Z.jpg/330px-Noel_28_oct_2007_1530Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Noel_28_oct_2007_1530Z.jpg/440px-Noel_28_oct_2007_1530Z.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Noel_28_oct_2007_1530Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Noel near Dominican Republic</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Dominican Republic, has some of the highest terrain surrounding the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, with Pico Duarte peaking at 10,700 feet (3,300 m) above sea level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Most of the tropical cyclone rainfall totals on the list below are 24‑hour maxima, which likely underrepresent the storm total.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Federated_States_of_Micronesia">Federated States of Micronesia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Federated States of Micronesia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chuuk">Chuuk</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Chuuk">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Elevations of the islands surrounding Chuuk lagoon reach a height of about 1,450 feet (440 m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Chataan" title="Typhoon Chataan">Typhoon Chataan</a> led to excessive rainfall on this island from June 23 – July 3, 2002, when a total of 939 mm (37.0 in) fell. During the time frame when Chataan was declared a tropical cyclone from July 1–3, 622 mm (24.5 in) fell, with 506 mm (19.9 in) falling on the 2nd alone at the international airport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PADGETTJUL2002_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTJUL2002-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_Chataan_07_july_2002_0150Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Yap_State">Yap State</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Yap State">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The wettest known tropical cyclone for the state was <a href="/wiki/1982_Pacific_typhoon_season#Typhoon_Ruby" title="1982 Pacific typhoon season">Ruby in 1982</a>, which drifted in the island's vicinity for several days during its initial development phase.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>

<p><a href="/wiki/Orography" title="Orography">Orography</a> from the volcanic islands of Fiji has led to significant rainfall during tropical cyclone passages, which occur roughly once a year.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Guadeloupe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hurricane Marilyn moved directly across the island in mid-September 1995,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marilyn_95_TCR_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marilyn_95_TCR-132">[132]</a></sup> bringing the highest known rainfall totals to the island from a tropical cyclone.</p>

<h3><span id="Réunion_Island"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="R.C3.A9union_Island">Réunion Island</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Réunion Island">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hyacinthe_25_jan_1980_0326Z_N6.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="580" data-file-width="600" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Hyacinthe_25_jan_1980_0326Z_N6.jpg/220px-Hyacinthe_25_jan_1980_0326Z_N6.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Hyacinthe_25_jan_1980_0326Z_N6.jpg/330px-Hyacinthe_25_jan_1980_0326Z_N6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Hyacinthe_25_jan_1980_0326Z_N6.jpg/440px-Hyacinthe_25_jan_1980_0326Z_N6.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hyacinthe_25_jan_1980_0326Z_N6.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cyclone Hyacinthe.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The mountainous island of Réunion has experienced several of the highest rainfall totals on record from tropical cyclones and holds the rainfall world records for 12, 24, 48, 72 hours, four, five, six, seven, eight, nine and ten days as a result.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gamede_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gamede-150">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-E4_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-E4-151">[151]</a></sup> The 12 and 24 hourly rainfall records were set at Foc-Foc by Cyclone Denise in 1966, while an Unnamed Tropical Cyclone between April 8–10, 1958 set the record for 48 hours at Aurere. <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Gamede" title="Cyclone Gamede">Tropical Cyclone Gamede</a> between February 24–28, 2007 came close to beating the records for 12, 24 and 48 hours before setting the records for three, four, five, six, seven, eight and nine days that were held by <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Hyacinthe" title="Cyclone Hyacinthe">Tropical Cyclone Hyacinthe</a> 1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gamede_150-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gamede-150">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-E4_151-1"><a href="#cite_note-E4-151">[151]</a></sup> Hyacinthe 1980 currently holds the world records for ten and fifteen days with rainfall totals of 5,678 millimetres (223.5 in) and 6,083 millimetres (239.5 in) respectively recorded at Commerson Crater.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-E4_151-2"><a href="#cite_note-E4-151">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bermuda">Bermuda</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Bermuda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bermuda has not historically received overwhelming rains out of tropical cyclones. This could be because of the rapid pace storms usually pass the island and the lack of mountains on the island.</p>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nicole_2016-10-12_1750Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="8400" data-file-width="6400" height="328" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Nicole_2016-10-12_1750Z.jpg/250px-Nicole_2016-10-12_1750Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Nicole_2016-10-12_1750Z.jpg/375px-Nicole_2016-10-12_1750Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Nicole_2016-10-12_1750Z.jpg/500px-Nicole_2016-10-12_1750Z.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Guatemala">Guatemala</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Guatemala">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Agatha_(2010)" title="Tropical Storm Agatha (2010)">Tropical Storm Agatha</a> in May 2010 became the second-wettest tropical cyclone in the nation's history when it slowly developed while remaining nearly stationary to the southwest of Guatemala, before turning northeast and dissipating across inland Central America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Agatha2010_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-Agatha2010-178">[178]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Haiti">Haiti</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Haiti">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Haiti that makes up three-eighths of Hispaniola,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> is a mountainous country that has experienced some of the most powerful hurricanes on record, including <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_David" title="Hurricane David">Hurricane David</a>. Its three mountain ranges have peaks as high as 8793 feet/2680 meters above sea level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gordon1994111400GOE7IR.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="230" data-file-width="220" height="230" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5d/Gordon1994111400GOE7IR.jpg" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gordon1994111400GOE7IR.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gordon dropping heavy rainfall on Haiti along its frontal-like band</div>
</div>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Indonesia">Indonesia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Indonesia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STC_Inigo_05_apr_2003_0625Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="8800" data-file-width="7200" height="269" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/STC_Inigo_05_apr_2003_0625Z.jpg/220px-STC_Inigo_05_apr_2003_0625Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/STC_Inigo_05_apr_2003_0625Z.jpg/330px-STC_Inigo_05_apr_2003_0625Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/STC_Inigo_05_apr_2003_0625Z.jpg/440px-STC_Inigo_05_apr_2003_0625Z.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STC_Inigo_05_apr_2003_0625Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cyclone Inigo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The precursor tropical disturbance of <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Inigo" title="Cyclone Inigo">Tropical Cyclone Inigo</a> in April 2003 dropped heavy rainfall in eastern Indonesia. The rainfall caused <a href="/wiki/Flash_flood" title="Flash flood">flash flooding</a> and mudslides, primarily in Flores but also on <a href="/wiki/West_Timor" title="West Timor">West Timor</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ocha1_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-ocha1-206">[206]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sumba" title="Sumba">Sumba</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bom_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-bom-207">[207]</a></sup> In some locations, the depth of the floodwaters reached 5 metres (16 ft). The Oessao River in <a href="/wiki/West_Timor" title="West Timor">West Timor</a> exceeded its banks, which flooded seven villages. In <a href="/wiki/Kupang" title="Kupang">Kupang</a> in West Timor, the system destroyed hundreds of homes and large fields of corn, bean, and rice crop. Heavy damage was reported near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ende,_Indonesia" title="Ende, Indonesia">Ende</a>, where flooding and mudslides destroyed 20 houses and destroyed the roads connecting to East Flores. The city airport was flooded with one meter (3 ft) of water, preventing aerial transportation and which left the city temporarily isolated. In <a href="/wiki/East_Flores_Regency" title="East Flores Regency">East Flores Regency</a> in eastern Flores Island, the system left 75 destroyed houses, along with 77 severely damaged and a further 56 receiving light damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ocha1_206-1"><a href="#cite_note-ocha1-206">[206]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable">
<caption>Wettest tropical cyclones and their remnants in Indonesia<br/>

</tr>

</tr>
<tr>
<td>1</td>
<td>223</td>
<td>8.78</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Inigo" title="Cyclone Inigo">Inigo 2003</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Larantuka" title="Larantuka">Larantuka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flores" title="Flores">Flores</a></td>

</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Jamaica">Jamaica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Jamaica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Michelle_2001.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="8800" data-file-width="6800" height="324" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Hurricane_Michelle_2001.jpg/250px-Hurricane_Michelle_2001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Hurricane_Michelle_2001.jpg/375px-Hurricane_Michelle_2001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Hurricane_Michelle_2001.jpg/500px-Hurricane_Michelle_2001.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Michelle_2001.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hurricane Michelle</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>This mountainous island country of Jamaica can get lashed with rainfall by slow-moving tropical cyclones in the western Caribbean Sea. Its interior, the Blue Mountains, reach a height of 7,400 feet (2,300 m) above sea level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Talas_Terra_MODIS_picture_2011-09-02_(High_Definition).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6828" data-file-width="7432" height="230" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Talas_Terra_MODIS_picture_2011-09-02_%28High_Definition%29.jpg/250px-Talas_Terra_MODIS_picture_2011-09-02_%28High_Definition%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Talas_Terra_MODIS_picture_2011-09-02_%28High_Definition%29.jpg/375px-Talas_Terra_MODIS_picture_2011-09-02_%28High_Definition%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Talas_Terra_MODIS_picture_2011-09-02_%28High_Definition%29.jpg/500px-Talas_Terra_MODIS_picture_2011-09-02_%28High_Definition%29.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Talas_Terra_MODIS_picture_2011-09-02_(High_Definition).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Severe Tropical Storm Talas approaching Japan on September 2, 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The mountainous island archipelago is constantly struck by typhoons recurving out of the tropics, which are normally in extratropical transition as they pass through Japan. Typhoon Namtheun of the <a href="/wiki/2004_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2004 Pacific typhoon season">2004 Pacific typhoon season</a> holds the national 24-hour precipitation record with 1,317 millimetres (51.9 in) observed in Kisawa village,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2004Japanrain_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-2004Japanrain-218">[218]</a></sup> surpassing the previous record of 1,140 mm (45 in) set during <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Fran" title="Typhoon Fran">Typhoon Fran</a> in 1976.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1976fran_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-1976fran-219">[219]</a></sup></p>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bolaven_Aug_26_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="9800" data-file-width="7600" height="322" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Bolaven_Aug_26_2012.jpg/250px-Bolaven_Aug_26_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Bolaven_Aug_26_2012.jpg/375px-Bolaven_Aug_26_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Bolaven_Aug_26_2012.jpg/500px-Bolaven_Aug_26_2012.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ryukyu_Islands">Ryukyu Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Ryukyu Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Rusa" title="Typhoon Rusa">Typhoon Rusa</a> caused 409 millimetres (16.1 in) of rain to fall at Naze on August 29–30, 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PADGETTAUG2002_231-1"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTAUG2002-231">[231]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Aere_(2004)" title="Typhoon Aere (2004)">Typhoon Aere</a> dropped 314.5 millimetres (12.38 in) of rain in the 65‑hour period ending at 1400 UTC on August 25, 2004 at Ishigakihima.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PADGETTAUG2004_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTAUG2004-74">[74]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/1957_Pacific_typhoon_season#Super_Typhoon_Agnes" title="1957 Pacific typhoon season">Typhoon Agnes</a> in August 1957 dropped 586.2 millimetres (23.08 in) of rainfall on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marcus_Island" title="Marcus Island">Marcus Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPCMAX_33-50"><a href="#cite_note-WPCMAX-33">[33]</a></sup> In 1972, <a href="/wiki/1972_Pacific_typhoon_season#Super_Typhoon_Rita_.28Gloring.29" title="1972 Pacific typhoon season">Typhoon Rita</a> dumped 31.87 in (809 mm) on <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Okinoerabu_Shima&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Okinoerabu Shima (page does not exist)">Okinoerabu Shima</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JTWC_Rita_1972_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-JTWC_Rita_1972-234">[234]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Johnston_Atoll">Johnston Atoll</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Johnston Atoll">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Tropical cyclones occasionally threaten this central Pacific island. Hurricane Celeste of 1972 brought 6.21 inches (158 mm) to the isle around August 19.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Korea">Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Korean_Peninsula" title="Korean Peninsula">Korean Peninsula</a> experiences typhoons regularly. Tropical cyclones which impact southern China also lead to, on average, five heavy rainfall events per year across the Korean peninsula.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Korea">North Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: North Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Very heavy rains fell across Tongchon and Kosong counties during <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Rusa" title="Typhoon Rusa">Typhoon Rusa</a> in 2002, where up to 510 millimetres (20 in) of precipitation fell in a 5- to 10-hour period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PADGETTAUG2002_231-2"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTAUG2002-231">[231]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Korea">South Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: South Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Madagascar">Madagascar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Madagascar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mexico_tropical_cyclone_rainfall_climatology" title="Mexico tropical cyclone rainfall climatology">Mexico tropical cyclone rainfall climatology</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Hurricane Wilma</a> of 2005 drifted over the northeast portion of the Yucatán peninsula for a couple of days, dropping significant rains. A report of 1,576 millimetres (62.0 in) was reported by the <a href="/wiki/Servicio_Meteorol%C3%B3gico_Nacional_(Mexico)" title="Servicio Meteorológico Nacional (Mexico)">Servicio Meteorológico Nacional</a> in Mexico,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup> which is the wettest known 24-hour rainfall amount ever measured in Mexico. Second on the list is from <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Frances_(1998)" title="Tropical Storm Frances (1998)">Tropical Storm Frances</a> in 1998, which accumulated up to 1,019 millimetres (40.1 in) of rain at Independencia in southern <a href="/wiki/Chiapas" title="Chiapas">Chiapas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup> Below is a list of the highest known storm total rainfall amounts from individual tropical cyclones across Mexico. Most of the rainfall information was provided by the Mexico's National Weather Service, Servicio Meteorológico Nacional, which is a part of the National Water Commission, <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Comisi%C3%B3n_Nacional_del_Agua&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Comisión Nacional del Agua (page does not exist)">Comisión Nacional del Agua</a></i>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mozambique">Mozambique</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Mozambique">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cyclone_Leon-Eline_22_feb_2000_0411Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="700" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Cyclone_Leon-Eline_22_feb_2000_0411Z.jpg/220px-Cyclone_Leon-Eline_22_feb_2000_0411Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Cyclone_Leon-Eline_22_feb_2000_0411Z.jpg/330px-Cyclone_Leon-Eline_22_feb_2000_0411Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Cyclone_Leon-Eline_22_feb_2000_0411Z.jpg/440px-Cyclone_Leon-Eline_22_feb_2000_0411Z.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cyclone_Leon-Eline_22_feb_2000_0411Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>

</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nepal">Nepal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Nepal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Some of the highest elevations on the planet lie in Nepal. Eight out of fourteen highest peaks in the world lie in the Nepalese Himalaya including the highest peak of the World, Mt. Everest (8848 m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup> During a tropical depression that affected the Indian Subcontinent in 2004, 51.3 millimetres (2.02 in) of rain fell at Kathmandu airport in the 24‑hour period ending at 1200 UTC on October 7.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PADGETTOCT2004_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTOCT2004-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands_Antilles">Netherlands Antilles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Netherlands Antilles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wilma_2011-01-26_0145Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6360" data-file-width="4770" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Wilma_2011-01-26_0145Z.jpg/220px-Wilma_2011-01-26_0145Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Wilma_2011-01-26_0145Z.jpg/330px-Wilma_2011-01-26_0145Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Wilma_2011-01-26_0145Z.jpg/440px-Wilma_2011-01-26_0145Z.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wilma_2011-01-26_0145Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cyclone Wilma (2011)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Most tropical cyclones which pass near New Zealand are in extratropical transition (ET) or have become extratropical, which can enhance their heavy rainfall threat.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Niue">Niue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Niue">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tropical_Cyclone_Heta_2004.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="8400" data-file-width="6400" height="328" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Tropical_Cyclone_Heta_2004.jpg/250px-Tropical_Cyclone_Heta_2004.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Tropical_Cyclone_Heta_2004.jpg/375px-Tropical_Cyclone_Heta_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Tropical_Cyclone_Heta_2004.jpg/500px-Tropical_Cyclone_Heta_2004.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tropical_Cyclone_Heta_2004.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cyclone Heta</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the passage of Tropical Cyclone Heta in January 2004, the Niue Meteorological Station reported a record 24-hour rainfall of 999.2 millimetres (39.34 in).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JAN2004_302-0"><a href="#cite_note-JAN2004-302">[302]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phet_jun_6_2010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2880" data-file-width="3840" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Phet_jun_6_2010.jpg/220px-Phet_jun_6_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Phet_jun_6_2010.jpg/330px-Phet_jun_6_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Phet_jun_6_2010.jpg/440px-Phet_jun_6_2010.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Phet_jun_6_2010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Phet" title="Cyclone Phet">Cyclone Phet</a>, a cyclone making landfall in Pakistan in June 2010 as a deep depression</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Tropical cyclones for the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Sea" title="Arabian Sea">Arabian Sea</a> usually affect Pakistan. Tropical cyclones from the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a> can affect Pakistan, though they usually weaken by the time they reach the Pakistani coastline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Palau">Palau</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: Palau">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_Mike_11_nov_1990_2221Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="740" data-file-width="648" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Typhoon_Mike_11_nov_1990_2221Z.jpg/220px-Typhoon_Mike_11_nov_1990_2221Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Typhoon_Mike_11_nov_1990_2221Z.jpg/330px-Typhoon_Mike_11_nov_1990_2221Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Typhoon_Mike_11_nov_1990_2221Z.jpg/440px-Typhoon_Mike_11_nov_1990_2221Z.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_Mike_11_nov_1990_2221Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Typhoon Mike</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Palau consists of a string of islands that is rugged and surrounds a lagoon. Elevations up to 2,060 feet (630 m) exist within the island group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Panama">Panama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: Panama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Inflow to the south of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Mitch" title="Hurricane Mitch">Hurricane Mitch</a> brought impressive rainfalls to the Panama. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Veledero_de_Tole&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Veledero de Tole (page does not exist)">Veledero de Tole</a> recorded 695 millimetres (27.4 in) of rainfall between October 22 and 31, 1998.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Typhoons_in_the_Philippines" title="Typhoons in the Philippines">Typhoons in the Philippines</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parma_oct_5_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7200" data-file-width="5600" height="283" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Parma_oct_5_2009.jpg/220px-Parma_oct_5_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Parma_oct_5_2009.jpg/330px-Parma_oct_5_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Parma_oct_5_2009.jpg/440px-Parma_oct_5_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parma_oct_5_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Typhoon Parma/Pepeng</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>This Philippines island archipelago is fairly mountainous, with the highest terrain found in Luzon.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Singapore">Singapore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=73" title="Edit section: Singapore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Vamei" title="Tropical Storm Vamei">Typhoon Vamei</a> of December 20, 2001 was the only known storm to ever hit the island state. It dropped 165.1 millimetres (6.50 in) of rainfall.</p>

<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BoM_TCR_339-0"><a href="#cite_note-BoM_TCR-339">[339]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa">South Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=75" title="Edit section: South Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Leon%E2%80%93Eline" title="Cyclone Leon–Eline">Tropical Cyclone Eline</a> in February 2000 dropped significant rains on portions of South Africa. The highest amount noted was 480 mm (19 in) at Thohoyandou.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-340"><a href="#cite_note-340">[340]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=76" title="Edit section: Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The only tropical cyclone to reach mainland Europe was 2005's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Vince_(2005)" title="Hurricane Vince (2005)">Hurricane Vince</a>. It dropped 3.3 inches (84 mm) of rain on the plain near Cordoba.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vince_rainfall_341-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vince_rainfall-341">[341]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sri_Lanka">Sri Lanka</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=77" title="Edit section: Sri Lanka">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/2004_North_Indian_Ocean_cyclone_season#Depression_BOB_04" title="2004 North Indian Ocean cyclone season">tropical depression</a> in early October 2004 led to heavy rains across Sri Lanka. The maximum was measured at Galle where 117.2 mm (4.61 in) fell in the 24‑hour period ending at 0600 UTC on the 2nd.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PADGETTOCT2004_42-3"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTOCT2004-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span id="St._Brandon,_South_Indian_Ocean"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="St._Brandon.2C_South_Indian_Ocean">St. Brandon, South Indian Ocean</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=78" title="Edit section: St. Brandon, South Indian Ocean">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_South-West_Indian_Ocean_cyclone_season#Severe_Tropical_Storm_Darius" title="2003–04 South-West Indian Ocean cyclone season">Tropical Cyclone Darius</a> of New Year's Eve/Day of 2003/2004 passed about 45 miles (72 km) west-northwest of the island. Rainfall over the 24‑hour period of closest approach was 135 mm (5.3 in).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PADGETTDEC2003_342-0"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTDEC2003-342">[342]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="St._Kitts_and_Nevis">St. Kitts and Nevis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=79" title="Edit section: St. Kitts and Nevis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=83" title="Edit section: Vanuatu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vania_13_January_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="12692" data-file-width="8857" height="315" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Vania_13_January_2011.jpg/220px-Vania_13_January_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Vania_13_January_2011.jpg/330px-Vania_13_January_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Vania_13_January_2011.jpg/440px-Vania_13_January_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Venezuela">Venezuela</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=84" title="Edit section: Venezuela">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A few tropical cyclones have skimmed the northern coast of South America over recent decades. <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bret_(1993)" title="Tropical Storm Bret (1993)">Tropical Storm Bret (1993)</a> dropped 339 millimetres (13.3 in) of rain in ten hours at <a href="/wiki/Guanare" title="Guanare">Guanare</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguesa_(state)" title="Portuguesa (state)">Portuguesa</a>, Venezuela.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-premlin1993_362-0"><a href="#cite_note-premlin1993-362">[362]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vietnam">Vietnam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=85" title="Edit section: Vietnam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
